{=Script - Textura semiquadrata=}\n
{=Status - MS punctuation done; tagging notes and textual notes up to date=}\n
{=Gaps between words are very small. Sometimes it is difficult to know\n
whether to record two words as joined or not, but I have made\n
judgements according to the spacing of immediately surrounding text I\n
have realised the yogh letter as z although it does often have the\n
general shape of insular g. But it seems to me to be formed in much\n
the same way as the scribe of Bodley 34 forms his and these can hardly\n
still be said to be insular g=}\n
{~f1r~}\n

indicating the originally mistaken word division=}\n

{.\'}\n
{=Wilson 1938 realises this as a punctus elevatus, but it is not the\n
usual kind. It looks more as if at the end of the line the scribe\n
erroneously began a third minim to make M instead of required N, then\n
realised his mistake and turned the half minim into the top oblique\n
stroke of a punctus elevatus and supplied the dot below it to cover his\n
error. None of the other versions have any punctuation at this point and\n
arguably it is not appropriate here=}\n
{\\}\n

$ruen/vps13_RUU+Ed $/vps13[N]_+Ed\n
{=Or read RUNEd "runs" Wilson (1938) reads RUUEd here but RUNEd in \n
Titus. He says (probably rightly) that RUNEd cannot be the correct\n
reading for semantic reasons and accepts Hall\'s (1928) suggestion that\n
RUUEd is from an otherwise unattested verb *ruuen related to "ruffle"\n
meaning "to stand on end". In fact the verb "ruff" is attested, albeit\n
only from C16, in the context of a hawk raising its feathers to a more\n
erect position. Here I follow MED\'s headword (from Bodley\'s RUEd) but\n
acknowledging that ruuen, rouen with intervocalic [v] is also possible=}\n

$gieldan/vSpt12_zULDE\n
{*sj context*}\n
{=d\'Ardenne & Dobson (1981) say that the yoghs on zEF and zULDE are\n
abnormal and \'a mixed letter\' between yogh and G.  The shape is nothing\n
like this scribe\'s normal Anglian two-compartment G which is made with\n
two bold bows in opposite directions and both closed, with the second\n
going well below the line and closed with a diagonal hairline, and with\n
a clear off-stroke on the right hand side of the first bow. THe yogh is\n
formed like a small Textura S at minim height and never goes below the\n
line. It has a decoratively waving top stroke in the shape of a modern\n
tilde. Occasionally this stroke is angled somewhat downwards from left\n
to right which is what has happened here. It is not especially abnormal\n
for this scribe=} \n
$&/cj_&\n

$nowhere/av-k_NOw+HwER $where/av-k_+HwER\n
{=NB this is a common form in the Titus texts. Titus has this apparently\n
diphthongal first element also at the same place in the running text\n
of St Katherine, and once later where Royal does not have it. But the\n
spelling also appears in Royal once in the Life of St Margaret. The\n
same kind of spellings happen also in the words "o:where", "o:whither"\n
and "nowhither" and they look to be forms common to whatever lies\n
behind T and R or, since it appears in all but one of T\'s texts, maybe\n
it\'s a NW Midland spelling and R has got it via the NW Midland version\n
behind T. Compare however Orm\'s OwwHAR and NAU+ spellings in Trinity\n
Homilies and Vices and Virtues in the East Midlands, and NOU+ spellings\n
in Laud Misc 108 hand A and the Nero version of Ancrene Riwle in the SW\n
Midlands=}\n
